# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Controller Manager Work Queue and Rate Limiting

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the controller work queue with rate limiting: the RateLimitingInterface, the ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter, the BucketRateLimiter, and the controller reconcile loop that uses Add/Get/Done for queue management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

47-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer at `/workspace/answer.json` that documents all the Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the controller work queue with rate limiting.

## Summary of Findings

I found **42 key files** organized in the following categories:

### Core Work Queue Infrastructure
1. **queue.go** - Base `TypedInterface` with `Add()`, `Get()`, `Done()` methods
2. **delaying_queue.go** - `TypedDelayingInterface` extending the queue with `AddAfter()`
3. **rate_limiting_queue.go** - `TypedRateLimitingInterface` with `AddRateLimited()`, `Forget()`, `NumRequeues()`
4. **default_rate_limiters.go** - Rate limiter implementations:
   - `TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter` (per-item exponential backoff)
   - `TypedBucketRateLimiter` (token bucket rate limiting)
   - `TypedMaxOfRateLimiter` (combines multiple limiters)
   - `DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter` (combines exponential + bucket)

### Controllers Using the Pattern
**25+ controller implementations** that use the work queue:
- Job, namespace, TTL, CronJob controllers
- Endpoint slice, node, route, service controllers
- Certificate, bootstrap, disruption controllers
- And many more across pkg/controller/ and staging/src/k8s.io/

### Key Architectural Pattern
The reconciliation loop implemented across all controllers:
1. `queue.Get()` - retrieves next item to process
2. `syncHandler()` - attempts to reconcile desired vs actual state
3. `queue.Done()` - marks item as processed
4. On success: `queue.Forget()` - stops retry tracking
5. On failure: `queue.AddRateLimited()` - requeues with backoff

The answer includes detailed symbols documentation and a comprehensive narrative explaining how all components integrate together in Kubernetes' control plane architecture.

Typed instead.\\n188: type Type = Typed[any]\\n189: \\n190: type Typed[t comparable] struct {\\n191: \\t// queue defines the order in which we will work on items. Every\\n192: \\t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\\n193: \\t// processing set.\\n194: \\tqueue Queue[t]\\n195: \\n196: \\t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\\n197: \\tdirty sets.Set[t]\\n198: \\n199: \\t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\\n200: \\t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. When we finish\\n201: \\t// processing something and remove it from this set, we'll check if\\n202: \\t// it's in the dirty set, and if so, add it to the queue.\\n203: \\tprocessing sets.Set[t]\\n204: \\n205: \\tcond *sync.Cond\\n206: \\n207: \\tshuttingDown bool\\n208: \\tdrain        bool\\n209: \\n210: \\tmetrics queueMetrics[t]\\n211: \\n212: \\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod time.Duration\\n213: \\tclock                      clock.WithTicker\\n214: \\n215: \\t// wg manages goroutines started by the queue to allow graceful shutdown\\n216: \\t// ShutDown() will wait for goroutines to exit before returning.\\n217: \\twg sync.WaitGroup\\n218: \\n219: \\tstopCh chan struct{}\\n220: \\t// stopOnce guarantees we only signal shutdown a single time\\n221: \\tstopOnce sync.Once\\n222: }\\n223: \\n224: // Add marks item as needing processing. You\\n254: // shouldn't e.g. gate a call to Add() or Get() on Len() being a particular\\n255: // value, that can't be synchronized properly.\\n256: func (q *Typed[T]) Len() int {\\n257: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n258: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n259: \\treturn q.queue.Len()\\n260: }\\n261: \\n262: // Get blocks until it can return an item to be processed. If shutdown = true,\\n263: // the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\\n264: // have finished processing it.\\n265: func (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\\n266: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n267: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n268: \\tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\\n269: \\t\\tq.cond.Wait()\\n270: \\t}\\n271: \\tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\\n272: \\t\\t// We must be shutting down.\\n273: \\t\\treturn *new(T), true\\n274: \\t}\\n275: \\n276: \\titem = q.queue.Pop()\\n277: \\n278: \\tq.metrics.get(item)\\n279: \\n280: \\tq.processing.Insert(item)\\n281: \\tq.dirty.Delete(item)\\n282: \\n283: \\treturn item, false\\n284: }\\n285: \\n286: // Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\\n287: // while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\\n288: // re-processing.\\n289: func (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\\n290: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n291: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n292: \\n293: \\tq.metrics.done(item)\\n294: \\n295: \\tq.processing.Delete(item)\\n296: \\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\\n297: \\t\\tq.queue.Push(item)\\n298: \\t\\tq.cond.Signal()\\n299: \\t} else if q.processing.Len() == 0 {\\n300: \\t\\tq.cond.Signal()\\n301: \\t}\\n302: }\\n303: \\n304: // ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. Worker\\n305: // goroutines will continue processing items in the queue until it is\\n306: // empty and then receive the shutdown signal.\\n307: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\\n308: \\tdefer false\\n317: \\tq.shuttingDown = true\\n318: \\tq.cond.Broadcast()\\n319: }\\n320: \\n321: // ShutDownWithDrain is equivalent to ShutDown but waits until all items\\n322: // in the queue have been processed.\\n323: // ShutDown can be called after ShutDownWithDrain to force\\n324: // ShutDownWithDrain to stop waiting.\\n325: // Workers must call Done on an item after processing it, If shutdown = true,\n263: // the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\n264: // have finished processing it.\n265: func (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\n266: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n267: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n268: \tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\n269: \t\tq.cond.Wait()\n270: \t}\n271: \tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\n272: \t\t// We must be shutting down.\n273: \t\treturn *new(T), true\n274: \t}\n275: \n276: \titem = q.queue.Pop()\n277: \n278: \tq.metrics.get(item)\n279: \n280: \tq.processing.Insert(item)\n281: \tq.dirty.Delete(item)\n282: \n283: \treturn item, false\n284: }\n285: \n286: // Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\n287: // while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\n288: // re-processing.\n289: func (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\n290: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n291: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n292: \n293: \tq.metrics.done(item)\n294: \n295: \tq.processing.Delete(item)\n296: \tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n297: \t\tq.queue.Push(item)\n298: \t\tq.cond.Signal()\n299: \t} else if q.processing.Len() == 0 {\n300: \t\tq.cond.Signal()\n301: \t}\n302: }\n303: \n304: // ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. Worker\n305: // goroutines will continue processing items in the queue until it is\n306: // empty and then receive the shutdown signal.\n307: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\n308: \tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n309: \tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n310: \t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n311: \t})\n312: \n313: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n314: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n315: \n316: \tq.drain = false\n317: \tq.shuttingDown = true\n318: \tq.cond.Broadcast()\n319: }\n320: \n321: // ShutDownWithDrain is equivalent to ShutDown but waits until all items\n322: // in the queue have been processed.\n323: // ShutDown can be called after ShutDownWithDrain to force\n324: // ShutDownWithDrain to stop waiting.\n325: // Workers must call Done on an item after processing it, otherwise\n326: // ShutDownWithDrain will block indefinitely.\n327: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDownWithDrain() {\n328: \tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n329: \tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n330: \t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n331: \t})\n332: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n333: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n334: \n335: \tq.drain = true\n336: \tq.shuttingDown = true\n337: \tq.cond.Broadcast()\n338: \n339: \tfor q.processing.Len() != 0 && q.drain {\n340: \t\tq.cond.Wait()\n341: \t}\n342: }\n343: \n344: func (q *Typed[T]) ShuttingDown() bool {\n345: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n346: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n347: \n348: \treturn q.shuttingDown\n349: }\n350: \n351: func (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWork() {\n352: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n353: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n354: \tif !q.shuttingDown {\n355: \t\tq.metrics.updateUnfinishedWork()\n356: \t}\n357: }\n358: \n359: func (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWorkLoop() {\n360: \tt := q.clock.NewTicker(q.unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod)\n361: \tdefer t.Stop()\n362: \tfor {\n363: \t\tselect {\n364: \t\tcase <-t.C():\n365: \t\t\tq.updateUnfinishedWork()\n366: \t\tcase <-q.stopCh:\n367: \t\t\treturn\n368: \t\t}\n369: \t}\n370: }\n371: ",

across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. The system is organized in a layered architecture:\\n\\n**Core Queue Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go):**\\nThe foundation is the TypedInterface which defines the basic work queue operations: Add(item), Get() returning (item, shutdown), Done(item), Len(), ShutDown(), and ShuttingDown(). The Typed[T] struct implements these with lock-based synchronization using sync.Cond, maintaining separate dirty and processing sets to handle concurrent access and re-enqueueing of items.\\n\\n**Delaying Queue (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go):**\\nThe TypedDelayingInterface extends TypedInterface by adding AddAfter(item, duration) capability, allowing items to be queued for later processing using a priority heap-based delay mechanism. This is essential for implementing backoff and retry logic.\\n\\n**Rate Limiting Queue (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go):**\\nThe TypedRateLimitingInterface further extends TypedDelayingInterface by adding rate limiting capabilities through three methods: AddRateLimited(item) which uses the rate limiter to determine when to process an item, Forget(item) to signal completion, and NumRequeues(item) to track retry counts. The rateLimitingType struct wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and TypedRateLimiter.\\n\\n**Rate Limiters (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):**\\nMultiple rate limiter implementations are provided:\\n- TypedRateLimiter is the base interface with When(item) returning time.Duration, Forget(item), and NumRequeues(item)\\n- TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter implements exponential backoff with baseDelay*2^failures capped at maxDelay\\n- TypedBucketRateLimiter adapts golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter for token bucket rate limiting\\n- TypedMaxOfRateLimiter combines multiple limiters taking the maximum delay\\n- TypedWithMaxWaitRateLimiter caps delays at a maximum threshold\\n- DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter combines ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter (per-item) with BucketRateLimiter (overall 10 qps, 100 bucket)\\n\\n**Reconciliation Loop Pattern:**\\nControllers implement the reconciliation pattern across numerous files. The sample controller (staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go) demonstrates the canonical pattern:\\n1. Run() launches worker goroutines calling runWorker()\\n2. runWorker() calls processNextWorkItem() in a loop\\n3. processNextWorkItem() implements the core cycle:\\n   - Call queue.Get() to retrieve next item, returns (item, shutdown)\\n   - Defer queue.Done(item) to mark item as processed\\n   - Call syncHandler(item) to reconcile desired vs actual state\\n   - On success: queue.Forget(item) to stop tracking retry count\\n   - On failure: queue.AddRateLimited(item) to requeue with backoff\\n\\nThis pattern is used across all controllers including: job_controller.go, namespace_controller.go, cronjob_controllerv2.go, endpointslice_controller.go, node_controller.go, route_controller.go, and many more in pkg/controller/ and staging/src/k8s.io/.\\n\\n**Key Design Principles:**\\n1. Queue operations are thread-safe and handle concurrent worker access\\n2. The dirty and processing sets prevent duplicate processing while allowing re-enqueueing\\n3. Rate limiting is applied both per-item (exponential backoff) and globally (token bucket)\\n4. The Forget() call is critical - without it, items remain in the rate limiter tracking indefinitely\\n5. Multiple workers can safely process different items in parallel while synchronizing through the shared queue\"\n}\n",
